  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a48295a3-b16b-4e2c-a17e-b51889db8145'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Arobynn had probably personally made sure he stayed dead. He would be a pretty bad King of Assassins if Sam is secretly alive. To answer your question<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Arobynn had probably personally made sure he stayed dead. He would be a pretty bad King of Assassins if Sam is secretly alive. To answer your question, he's not coming back, the book said he was tortured to death. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15763285-the-assassin-and-the-empire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1393092425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3206364216187053874"><i>
  <b>“My name is Celaena Sardothien, and I will not be afraid.”</b>
</i> <br/><br/>This novella was too much for me to take. I knew it was coming but still, it left me utterly unprepared for what happened to <b>Celaena</b> and <b>Sam</b>. It was just so heartbreaking and painful. Everything was brutal I’m so surprised to find myself being able to handle it without breaking my heart into tiny bits of pieces.<br/><br/>I’ve read <b>Throne of Glass</b> prior to reading this and now everything already made a perfect sense. What happened to Celaena wa</span>
  <span id="freeText3206364216187053874" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“My name is Celaena Sardothien, and I will not be afraid.”</b>
</i> <br /><br />This novella was too much for me to take. I knew it was coming but still, it left me utterly unprepared for what happened to <b>Celaena</b> and <b>Sam</b>. It was just so heartbreaking and painful. Everything was brutal I’m so surprised to find myself being able to handle it without breaking my heart into tiny bits of pieces.<br /><br />I’ve read <b>Throne of Glass</b> prior to reading this and now everything already made a perfect sense. What happened to Celaena was so unbearable. Now I understand why it was hard for her to keep herself together whenever she remembers her past, especially the part where she was betrayed by someone she couldn’t point out.<br /><br />After reading this novella, I felt the rage Celeana endured and the need to find justice and revenge. I also felt hopeful that somehow Celaena will be able to avenge herself and Sam. Despite the horrible things that happened to her in this novella, everything was perfectly executed by Sarah J. Maas. I couldn’t stop myself admiring her writing style that can absolutely carry me away and basically steal my heart and wrap myself with so many emotions.<br /><br />Rating: 5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="3206364216187053874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2525007433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7835507623978091260"><u>5 STAR'S</u> <br/><br/><i>“She didn't want to go out into a world where he didn't exist. So she watched the light shift and change, and let the world pass by without her.”</i><br/><br/>Wow, this was another awesome and final novella in the <i>Throne of Glass</i> series. I thoroughly enjoyed reading <i>The Assassin and the Empire</i> very very much :) It was addicting and I couldn't read it fast enough. I love all the sweet moments in Celaena's apartment with Sam. Sam is quite the catch and there is no way in hell you can't fall in love wit</span>
  <span id="freeText7835507623978091260" style="display:none"><u>5 STAR'S</u> <br><br><i>“She didn't want to go out into a world where he didn't exist. So she watched the light shift and change, and let the world pass by without her.”</i><br><br>Wow, this was another awesome and final novella in the <i>Throne of Glass</i> series. I thoroughly enjoyed reading <i>The Assassin and the Empire</i> very very much :) It was addicting and I couldn't read it fast enough. I love all the sweet moments in Celaena's apartment with Sam. Sam is quite the catch and there is no way in hell you can't fall in love with the guy. And even though I knew it was coming it did absolutely nothing to soften the BLOW to my heart! The ending was one of the saddest damn endings I've read in this series and I don't know how I'll ever recover. I'm broken and even kinda mad at this point. Even if you know what Sam's fate is going to be before this it's obvious that the mission is gonna be a complete and utter failure, also even before you learn of the setup. But still, I really wished this could have had a different outcome and at the same time if this didn't happen I wouldn't have Rowan and well... I just wouldn't be cool with that. Anyways I love all the action and even though this left a gaping hole in my chest it's still one of my favorites and therefore it's also a must-read. <br><br><i>“She would tuck Sam into her heart, a bright light for her to take out whenever things were darkest. And then she would remember how it had felt to be loved, when the world had held nothing but possibility. No matter what they did to her, they could never take that away.”</i><br><br><b><i>“My name is Celaena Sardothien,”</i> she whispered, <i>“and I will not be afraid.”</i><b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479218591ra/21161613.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b></b></span>

  <span id="freeText7663839768771965109" style="display:none"><b><u>Lavender soap.</u> Such a tiny but heart-rending detail. </b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Q:<br />The body still smelled faintly like Sam. And like the cheap soap she’d made him use, because she was so selfish that she couldn’t let him have her lavender soap. (c) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>An essay on the consequences of misplaced trust and Electra complex and lack of readiness to face the treacherous world. An interesting combo to ponder.<br /><br />PS. Well, they should have ran. Regardless of libraries, perfumes, hot water, secrets and other rickrack. Hindsight, 20/20. </b><br /><br />Q:<br />The word was just another weapon. (c)<br />Q:<br />She was … responsible for him now. And that was terrifying. (c)<br />Q:<br />He was hers. This magnificent, powerful creature was hers. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Whenever I’m scared out of my wits, I tell myself: My name is Sam Cortland … and I will not be afraid. I’ve been doing it for years. ”...<br />“Maybe I should try your little trick.” She took another breath. “My name is Celaena Sardothien, and I will not be afraid.” ...<br />“I think you have to say it with a bit more conviction than that.” (с)<br />Q:<br />then he surprised Celaena once by going into a bookshop—not to threaten the owner or collect dues, but to buy books.<br />She’d hated that, for some reason. Especially when, despite Sam’s protests, she’d quickly snuck in while the bookseller was in the back and spied the receipt ledger behind the desk. Farran hadn’t bought books about torture or death or anything wicked. Oh, no. They’d been adventure novels. Novels that she had read and enjoyed. The idea of Farran reading them too felt like a violation, somehow. (c)<br />Q:<br />She wondered if it was better to wind up as a slave here, or a prisoner in a brutal labor camp like Endovier. Both seemed like similar versions of a living hell. (c) Nice touch with foreshadowing.<br />Q:<br />But this place is designed like a death trap, and I’ve no desire to make my final stand here, or right now. (с)<br />Q:<br />Sam would never be like Farran. He’d never be like her, either. She sometimes wondered if he knew just how dark she could turn. (c)<br />Q:<br />We know how to do it, but we don’t enjoy it. That’s the difference. ...<br />“When we die, do you think we’ll be punished for the things we’ve done?”... <br />“When we die, ... I don’t think the gods will even know what to do with us.” (c)<br />Q:<br />There was no end to this silence. There would never be an end, only this beginning. (c)<br />Q:<br />...she’d stop at nothing to find him. And then she’d slaughter them all. (c)<br />Q:<br />Reality opened wide and swallowed her whole. ...<br />She didn’t want to go out into a world where he didn’t exist. So she watched the light shift and change, and let the world pass by without her. (c)<br />Q:<br />She was fire, she was darkness, she was dust and blood and shadow. (c)<br />Q:<br />When the roaring silence came to claim her again, Celaena walked into it with open arms. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Whatever gutter you grew up in, Farran, it must have been an unparalleled sort of hell.” ...<br />“You have no idea.” ...<br />“Why did you do it?” ...<br />“Because I don’t like sharing my belongings.” (c)<br />Q:<br />Pine and snow and lazy, golden summers—a city of light and music in the shadow of the Staghorn Mountains. ...<br />The breeze grew into a wind, and she closed her eyes, letting it sweep away the ashes of that dead world—of that dead girl. And then there was nothing left except something new, something still glowing red from the forging. ...<br />She would go into Endovier. Go into Hell. And she would not crumble. ...<br />She had not stopped breathing yet, and she had endured Sam’s death and evaded the king’s execution. She would survive this. ...<br />She would tuck Sam into her heart, a bright light for her to take out whenever things were darkest. And then she would remember how it had felt to be loved, when the world had held nothing but possibility. No matter what they did to her, they could never take that away.<br />She would not break. (c)<br />Q:</span>

  <blockquote>“She didn't want to go out into a world where he didn't exist. So she watched the light shift and change, and let the world pass by without her.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486096645i/21881156._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The tension built up since The Assassin and the Underworld. I read this book with a shaking heart even if I knew that the ending was not that bad, I still shocked when I was on the last page. Sam and Calaene take a new mission, which is abnormally hard for every assassion. Yet she thinks she can do it, and that will gain lots of money and it's enough for them to start their new lives.<br><br>Arobynn is a treacherous bastard since the first book. His scheme is not perfect but tricky enough to lure Celaena in. Sam, on the other hand, is tremendously changed. I had no idea why he was so different, but indeed he was.<br><br>The ending literally tore my apart, but I was glad that it ended like this.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“When we die," she said, "I don't think the gods will even know what to do with us.”</blockquote>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1363525439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6828646849304451626"><b>
  <blockquote>" “I can wait,” he said thickly, kissing her collarbone. “We have all the time in the world.” "</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>This book is written to torture the heart. Every word and sentence is that much more heartbreaking because you <i>know</i> what's going to happen! You know how this young couple's dream of peace and love is going to end!<br/>I hate this book for what it did to my soul. And love it, because unlike other prequel short stories written to show events that happened before the first book in the series, this one actu</span>
  <span id="freeText6828646849304451626" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>" “I can wait,” he said thickly, kissing her collarbone. “We have all the time in the world.” "</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />This book is written to torture the heart. Every word and sentence is that much more heartbreaking because you <i>know</i> what's going to happen! You know how this young couple's dream of peace and love is going to end!<br />I hate this book for what it did to my soul. And love it, because unlike other prequel short stories written to show events that happened before the first book in the series, this one actually has a purpose. It actually feels like an integral part of the series instead of a ploy to get more money by milking a series.<br /><br />This book shattered my heart into a thousand pieces. But at the same time, it gave me a closer look at what Celaena had to endure to get to where she is and how she became who she is. And I loved and loved and loved it. I think after this a reread of the series is in order before I tackle the 6th book and torture my soul all over again.<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>"And then she would remember how it had felt to be loved, when the world had held nothing but possibility. No matter what they did to her, they could never take that away.<br />She would not break."</blockquote>
  <br />
</b><br />This series will forever be one of my favorites and I'm sure I will keep coming back for rereads as I undoubtedly forget many parts of it. The feeling and sensation of this book, however, will stay with me forever.<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>" “My name is Celaena Sardothien,” she whispered, “<i>and I will not be afraid.</i>” "</blockquote>
</b></span>

<div id="review_374757210" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/374757210" />
    <a title="Alz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4781184-alz"><img alt="Alz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294641567p2/4781184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/374757210?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alz" href="/user/show/4781184-alz">Alz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4781184-alz?shelf=ya-mg">ya-mg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4781184-alz?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer374757210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16025396459180971975">A little novella in which nothing happens except things that Celaena could have avoided if she hadn't been so incredibly blindly stupid. She underwent no character growth, faced no real challenges except trumped-up excuses for plot, and acted so frivolous that it's no surprise that she ends up where she does.<br/><br/>For another thing, aspects of this book are way, way too modern--and I mean yes, this IS fantasy and all, but when it's set in Ye Elde Generic Fantasyland, I find it a bit much for her to ha</span>
  <span id="freeText16025396459180971975" style="display:none">A little novella in which nothing happens except things that Celaena could have avoided if she hadn't been so incredibly blindly stupid. She underwent no character growth, faced no real challenges except trumped-up excuses for plot, and acted so frivolous that it's no surprise that she ends up where she does.<br /><br />For another thing, aspects of this book are way, way too modern--and I mean yes, this IS fantasy and all, but when it's set in Ye Elde Generic Fantasyland, I find it a bit much for her to have an apartment that has a fully-stocked kitchen, bedroom, bathroom, and living room with floor-to-ceiling glass windows, running water, etc. And when discussion arises about moving away from Rifthold, they talk about moving with just the basics in luggage and having everything else shipped to them, and how they can just sell the apartment while they're away by...apparently writing letters to some kind of broker.<br /><br />But back to the lack of plot and Celaena's stupidity. 100% of everything bad that happens in this book could have been avoided if Celaena had either bothered to listen to other people or just stopped spending their rapidly decreasing amount of money on lavender soap and frilly designer outfits--especially since (as it's revealed at the beginning) she and Sam haven't been able to find work for a month and are running low on funds. Also, I couldn't stand how head-bangingly stupid she was RE: Arobynn, a man who (she is aware) has manipulated her all her life, beaten her unconscious as "punishment", deceived her and tricked her and humiliated her, used her for his own ends that she hated, etc. etc., and yet whom she still trusts and takes at face value despite all her "oh noes, I don't trust him, of course" talk.<br /><br />I barely tolerated Celaena's stupidity for 3 novellas before this and now I just can't stand it, which is why this is a 1-star. While not as depressingly terrible as the previous novella, this one exists solely to get her thrown into the terrible straits where the novel begins--in other words, this novella is much more a plot device than a novella.<br /><br />Even the emotional parts of this book felt lackluster and contrived, to the point where I was bored and rolling my eyes when Terrible Things happened. Everything was too rushed, Celaena's responses were either hyperbolically exaggerated or bizarrely nonsensical (i.e. how she nags Sam to stop fighting for prize money because omg he might get hurt when hey, Celaena, HE'S A FRICKING ASSASSIN AND CAN TAKE CARE OF HIMSELF AND YOU NEED MONEY BECAUSE YOU'RE BUYING EXPENSIVE PERFUMES AND FURNITURE ON A SHOESTRING BUDGET AND YOU DON'T BRING IN ANY MONEY AT ALL), and the final plot twists in the end were so incredibly obvious I was wondering if they were going to be something else because it was way too obvious but nope, that was it.<br /><br />I really wanted to read Throne of Glass before but these novellas are seriously putting me off reading the novel. But because I am masochistic and I have nostalgic memories of reading Throne of Glass when it was on Fictionpress many years ago, when I was younger and less jaded and critical, I will probably read the novel anyway. And then gripe about it afterward.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16025396459180971975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=strong-emotions">strong-emotions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=great-fighting-scenes">great-fighting-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=ebooks-ibooks">ebooks-ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=sad-stories">sad-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1282079598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13543486794951368010"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443500326i/16369141.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was certainly a heart-shattering story and Sam's death was unfathomably painful to me. The beginning of it was too dreamy to be true, the way Sam and Celaena believed in the possibility of leaving Rifthold and starting their new life without the control of either Arobynn Hamel or the Assassins' Guild; however, the ending was something entirely unexpected. Such a dramatic twist was hard to endure, honestly. <br/><br/>Although the killing scenes were bloody as usual, I think the Crime Lord of Rifthold </span>
  <span id="freeText13543486794951368010" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443500326i/16369141.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was certainly a heart-shattering story and Sam's death was unfathomably painful to me. The beginning of it was too dreamy to be true, the way Sam and Celaena believed in the possibility of leaving Rifthold and starting their new life without the control of either Arobynn Hamel or the Assassins' Guild; however, the ending was something entirely unexpected. Such a dramatic twist was hard to endure, honestly. <br><br>Although the killing scenes were bloody as usual, I think the Crime Lord of Rifthold was truly sadistic. Imagine a <i>human being</i> enjoying torturing his victims and playing with their corpses until they didn't have any blood to splatter. Farren disgusted me most, for his unmeasurable cruelty and extreme brutality, and his sick personality. And again, Celaena fell right into their(Arobynn and Farren's) <i>little</i> trap just like her last time. I felt pity for her but also secretly hoped that she'd listened to Wesley's warning or at least didn't allow Sam to dispatch the notorious Crime Lord. So many things/accidents would be avoided if she thought twice before she leaped. The story left me with a lot of what-ifs but I guess some are just...inevitable and her fate was doomed because of the ones who betrayed her could benefit most once she was gone. <br><br>Therefore, the last of the novellas was just the beginning of Celaena's suffering and it was surly not a happy ending. You know, everything has its price to pay and she's got to be responsible for all the lives she took during her notoriously proud "Adarlan's Assassin" moments. The reality will swallow her wholly and it's time for her to <s>seek revenge</s> face the music. But I know she's going to survive the so-called death camp, Endovier, because there'll always be a beloved person carved into her deepest mind and he'll still serve as a reminder for her to stay alive. I also believe that there's a possibility after all this mess is eliminated. As an old saying goes, <i>
  <u>Every cloud has a silver lining.</u>
</i> <br><b>
  <blockquote>She would tuck Sam into her heart, a bright light for her to take out whenever things were darkest. And then she would remember how it had felt to be loved, when the world had held nothing but possibility. No matter what they did to her, they could never take that away.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I'll miss you forever, Sam Cortland.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443500326i/16369142._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13543486794951368010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14075424749676096040">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br/><br/>I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. I am not a huge fan of novellas, but I do know that some of the characters introduced in the last book were first introduced in some of these novellas in <b>The Assassin'</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14075424749676096040" style="display:none">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br><br>I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. And because I love <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3433047.Sarah_J_Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah J. Maas's</a>
</b> story telling and her writing, I am going to go ahead and read these beauties.<br><br>So, with that said, I am going to read and rate these so I can finally be completely caught up on The Throne of Glass Series: Throne of Glass, Crown of Midnight, Heir of Fire, Queen of Shadows, Empire of Storms, and Tower of Dawn.<br><br><u>The Assassin and the Empire (Throne of Glass, #0.5)</u><br>Heart is ripped out and barely beating on the table in front of me.<br><br>This is absolutely horrible. Maas just wanted to make us sob for days. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512946301ra/24649449.gif" alt="" width="350" height="140" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Like I feel as if Aelin/Celaena should have brought down more hell than she did in the series. She is the fire-breathing QUEEN. Arobynn deserved what he got (in the books, not in the novellas which would just be a lot of money basically) and like a thousand times more. <br><br>You don't like sharing your things? Well Aelin should have showed you just how much of "your thing" she is. For the life of me.<br><br>On the other side of things, this is me every time I see Lysandra<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512946301ra/24649450.gif" alt="" width="350" height="188" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Like she's pretty awful in these novellas but I still kind of love her.<br><br>I just can't bring myself to talk about this one. I'm sorry but really I'm not because if you can talk about what happened in this book you don't have a beating heart.</span>

To Sam.”</b>

<div id="review_3456835674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3456835674" />
    <a title="Beenish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106139933-beenish"><img alt="Beenish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594382336p2/106139933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3456835674?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beenish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beenish" href="/user/show/106139933-beenish">Beenish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3456835674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15204922308766587333">4.5★<br/><br/>This is the last novella and the only one that starts with a warning vibe and mentally prepares you for what may come ahead.<br/><br/>𝙃𝙚'𝙙 𝙝𝙤𝙣𝙚𝙙 𝙝𝙚𝙧 𝙖𝙣𝙜𝙚𝙧 𝙞𝙣𝙩𝙤 𝙖 𝙡𝙚𝙩𝙝𝙖𝙡 𝙗𝙡𝙖𝙙𝙚. 𝘼𝙣𝙙 𝙨𝙝𝙚'𝙙 𝙡𝙚𝙩 𝙝𝙞𝙢.<br/><br/>Previously, the novellas were all about missions and punishments, betrayals and the sorting of emotions. <br/>While this novella brings us mind games and the fire of revenge. <br/>Not only that, we also learn more about the characters, how their mind works, what they feel, what breaks them most, how after broken trust, f</span>
  <span id="freeText15204922308766587333" style="display:none">4.5★<br /><br />This is the last novella and the only one that starts with a warning vibe and mentally prepares you for what may come ahead.<br /><br />𝙃𝙚'𝙙 𝙝𝙤𝙣𝙚𝙙 𝙝𝙚𝙧 𝙖𝙣𝙜𝙚𝙧 𝙞𝙣𝙩𝙤 𝙖 𝙡𝙚𝙩𝙝𝙖𝙡 𝙗𝙡𝙖𝙙𝙚. 𝘼𝙣𝙙 𝙨𝙝𝙚'𝙙 𝙡𝙚𝙩 𝙝𝙞𝙢.<br /><br />Previously, the novellas were all about missions and punishments, betrayals and the sorting of emotions. <br />While this novella brings us mind games and the fire of revenge. <br />Not only that, we also learn more about the characters, how their mind works, what they feel, what breaks them most, how after broken trust, faith remains there when some people are the only people you know. Like 𝗔𝗿𝗼𝗯𝘆𝗻𝗻. <br />He plays dirty games and tricks you so cleanly and above all that, reminds you who has power and who, in the end, will win. He messes with everyone and those who mess with him are very badly ruined.<br /><br />𝙎𝙝𝙚 𝙨𝙤𝙢𝙚𝙩𝙞𝙢𝙚𝙨 𝙬𝙤𝙣𝙙𝙚𝙧𝙚𝙙 𝙞𝙛 𝙝𝙚 𝙠𝙣𝙚𝙬 𝙟𝙪𝙨𝙩 𝙝𝙤𝙬 𝙙𝙖𝙧𝙠 𝙨𝙝𝙚 𝙘𝙤𝙪𝙡𝙙 𝙩𝙪𝙧𝙣.<br /><br />In this novella, we all get what we wanted so much. Some 𝗖𝗲𝗹𝗮𝗲𝗻𝗮 and 𝗦𝗮𝗺 moments.<br /><br />𝙎𝙝𝙚’𝙙 𝙝𝙖𝙫𝙚 𝙩𝙤 𝙡𝙚𝙖𝙫𝙚 𝙝𝙚𝙧 𝙛𝙪𝙧𝙣𝙞𝙩𝙪𝙧𝙚 𝙖𝙣𝙙 𝙢𝙤𝙨𝙩 𝙤𝙛 𝙝𝙚𝙧 𝙨𝙝𝙤𝙚𝙨 𝙗𝙚𝙝𝙞𝙣𝙙 𝙛𝙤𝙧 𝙣𝙤𝙬, 𝙗𝙪𝙩 𝙩𝙝𝙚𝙧𝙚 𝙬𝙖𝙨 𝙣𝙤 𝙬𝙖𝙮 𝙞𝙣 𝙝𝙚𝙡𝙡 𝙨𝙝𝙚 𝙬𝙖𝙨 𝙜𝙤𝙞𝙣𝙜 𝙩𝙤 𝙢𝙤𝙫𝙚 𝙩𝙤 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙨𝙤𝙪𝙩𝙝𝙚𝙧𝙣 𝙘𝙤𝙣𝙩𝙞𝙣𝙚𝙣𝙩 𝙬𝙞𝙩𝙝𝙤𝙪𝙩 𝙖𝙡𝙡 𝙤𝙛 𝙝𝙚𝙧 𝙗𝙤𝙤𝙠𝙨.<br /><br />Yes, both 𝗦𝗮𝗺 and 𝗖𝗲𝗹𝗮𝗲𝗻𝗮 decide to go away. Leave Arobynn behind and start a new life but do you think he'd let them go so easily? Someone told Celaena "𝘌𝘷𝘦𝘳𝘺𝘵𝘩𝘪𝘯𝘨 𝘩𝘢𝘴 𝘢 𝘱𝘳𝘪𝘤𝘦" but whatever they paid Arobynn wasn't the actual price.<br /><br />𝙎𝙝𝙚 𝙬𝙤𝙪𝙡𝙙 𝙣𝙤𝙩 𝙗𝙧𝙚𝙖𝙠.<br /><br />This novella is very sad. But I liked it. I'll be writing about the characters on 𝑻𝒉𝒆 𝑨𝒔𝒔𝒂𝒔𝒔𝒊𝒏'𝒔 𝑩𝒍𝒂𝒅𝒆's review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15204922308766587333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1703658979294483011" style="display:none">I think this was the most haunting of all the short stories. We see Celaena and Sam falling in love, we witness Arobynn's obsession and revenge on Celaena, see her lose someone she loves, gets betrayed again and sent to Endovier;the one thing that made me halt is my suspension that Arobynn and the King knew who she truly was and that's why they didn't want anyone to see her. Honestly, anyone should read these, whether they have read any of the throne of glass books or not. </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_26032912'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032912-the-queen-of-nothing"><img alt="The Queen of Nothing (The Folk of the Air, #3)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1553624975l/26032912._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UeSdU3Z0N5NGLsB2aCQCSwJH7gA/BJv1H44xuUwntvRWj9x8z1y4qtCjeTbpfaoMSX2N2U8DqA1nNgL31MarJA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
